            <div style="padding:3px 3px 0 0; font-family:sans-serif; font-size:120%; color:#000; border-bottom:1px solid; border-bottom-color:#8B0000; background:transparent;">
             Welcome to the Village pump
            </div> <p>This page is used for discussions of the operations, technical issues, and policies of Wikimedia Commons. Recent sections with no replies for 7 days and sections tagged with <kbd>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Section_resolved" title="Template:Section resolved">Section resolved</a>|1=--~~~~}}</kbd> may be archived; for old discussions, see the <b><a href="/wiki/Commons:Village_pump/Archive" title="Commons:Village pump/Archive">archives</a></b>; the latest archive is <a href="/wiki/Commons:Village_pump/Archive/2021/05" title="Commons:Village pump/Archive/2021/05">Commons:Village pump/Archive/2021/05</a>. </p><p>Please note: </p> 
            <hr> 
            <ol>
             <li>If you want to ask why unfree/non-commercial material is not allowed at Wikimedia Commons or if you want to suggest that allowing it would be a good thing, please <i>do not</i> comment here. It is probably pointless. One of Wikimedia Commons’ core principles is: "Only <a href="/wiki/Commons:Licensing" title="Commons:Licensing">free content</a> is allowed." This is a basic rule of the place, as inherent as the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WP:NPOV" class="extiw" title="w:WP:NPOV">NPOV</a> requirement on all Wikipedias.</li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:FAQ" title="Commons:FAQ">Have you read our <i>FAQ</i>?</a></li> 
             <li>For changing the name of a file, see <a href="/wiki/Commons:File_renaming" title="Commons:File renaming">Commons:File renaming</a>.</li> 
             <li>Any answers you receive here are not legal advice and the responder cannot be held liable for them. If you have legal questions, we can try to help but our answers cannot replace those of a qualified professional (i.e. a lawyer).</li> 
             <li>Your question will be answered here; please check back regularly. Please do not leave your email address or other contact information, as this page is widely visible across the internet and you are liable to receive spam.</li>
            </ol> <p>Purposes which do not meet the scope of this page: </p> 
            <hr> 
            <ul>
             <li>Please do not make <i>deletion requests</i> here: use <a href="/wiki/Commons:DR" class="mw-redirect" title="Commons:DR"><i>the relevant process for it</i></a> instead.</li> 
             <li>For <i>technical support and graphics talks</i> (PNG, SVG, GIF, etc.), please post on the <a href="/wiki/Commons:Graphics_village_pump" title="Commons:Graphics village pump"><i>Graphics village pump</i></a>.</li> 
             <li>To ask for <i>image improvement</i>, see: 
              <ul>
               <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Graphic_Lab/Photography_workshop" title="Commons:Graphic Lab/Photography workshop">Graphic Lab/Photography workshop</a> for photographs.</li> 
               <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Graphic_Lab/Map_workshop" title="Commons:Graphic Lab/Map workshop">Graphic Lab/Map workshop</a> for maps.</li> 
               <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Graphic_Lab/Illustration_workshop" title="Commons:Graphic Lab/Illustration workshop">Graphic Lab/Illustration workshop</a> for other illustrations.</li>
              </ul></li> 
             <li>To ask for <i>video or audio improvement</i>, see <a href="/wiki/Commons:Graphic_Lab/Video_and_sound_workshop" title="Commons:Graphic Lab/Video and sound workshop">Commons:Graphic Lab/Video and sound workshop</a>.</li> 
             <li>For <i>translation requests</i>, please post at <a href="/wiki/Commons:Requests_for_translation" title="Commons:Requests for translation">Commons:Requests for translation</a>.</li> 
             <li>For <i>photograph requests</i>, please post at <a href="/wiki/Commons:Picture_requests" class="mw-redirect" title="Commons:Picture requests">Commons:Picture requests</a>.</li>
            </ul> <p>Search archives: </p>

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_05">May 05</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: May 05">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Category:Tones_and_I">Category:Tones and I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Category:Tones and I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
       <p>I've asked for help at <a href="/wiki/Commons_talk:Categories#Category:Tones_and_I" title="Commons talk:Categories">Commons talk:Categories#Category:Tones and I</a> on 30 April 2021 but have received no reply. At the Category:Tones and I page there is an infobox, it contains contentious information, specifically: year of birth, date of birth and middle name. This information is not supported by reliable sources and may violate WP:BLPPRIVACY. How can this be removed from that infobox? According to policy it should be removed immediately.<a href="/wiki/User:Shaidar_cuebiyar" title="User:Shaidar cuebiyar">Shaidar cuebiyar</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Shaidar_cuebiyar" title="User talk:Shaidar cuebiyar"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 04:45, 5 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <ul>
        <li>@<a href="/wiki/User:Shaidar_cuebiyar" title="User:Shaidar cuebiyar">Shaidar cuebiyar</a>: For the future: it might have been better to ask at <a href="/wiki/Category_talk:Tones_and_I" title="Category talk:Tones and I">Category talk:Tones and I</a> than <a href="/wiki/Commons_talk:Categories#Category:Tones_and_I" title="Commons talk:Categories">Commons talk:Categories#Category:Tones and I</a>.</li> 
        <li>All of that info comes from the wikidata item <a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q62887629" class="extiw" title="d:Q62887629"><span title="Australian musician">Tones and I <small>(Q62887629)</small></span></a>. Date of birth is referenced there. Anyway, if you have references to the contrary, Wikidata would be the place to take it up. I don't think privacy can possibly apply to information cited from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NRJ" class="extiw" title="en:NRJ">NRJ</a>. - <a href="/wiki/User:Jmabel" title="User:Jmabel">Jmabel</a>&nbsp;! <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jmabel" title="User talk:Jmabel">talk</a> 15:05, 5 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <ul>
          <li>Thanks for the heads up. The NRJ article does not give her birth date. The closest it comes is repeating the claim, seen in Australian media, that she was 19 at the time of a performance (not precisely dated nor verified by the artist or management). There is no indication of a middle name here. The NRJ cites from an unnamed article in <i>The Sydney Morning Herald</i>.</li> 
          <li>Nick Bond of <i>news.com.au</i> is cited at wikidata for her birth date. However that article presents this as a claim by other media outlets and also discusses another date put forward. Note: the English WP article has had both dates at different times but neither (nor other contenders) has been supported by the artist/managers. There is no indication of her middle name.</li> 
          <li>I believe wikidate has it wrong and will try there, next.<a href="/wiki/User:Shaidar_cuebiyar" title="User:Shaidar cuebiyar">Shaidar cuebiyar</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Shaidar_cuebiyar" title="User talk:Shaidar cuebiyar"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 01:27, 10 May 2021 (UTC) 
           <ul>
            <li>Good if you know your ways around there or otherwise can do what has to be done. Usually what has to be done on Wikidata is to give dubious facts a lower "rank".</li>
           </ul> 
           <dl>
            <dd>
             Over here, we can choose what data is selected for display in the infobox. On Swedish Wiukipedia there has been much discussion on the issue, and one thing that has been done is to exclude data without source (or just citing Wikipedia) and data with lower rank. The infoboxes also allow for overruling wikidata with explicit parameters. I don't know how the template over here works.
            </dd> 
            <dd>
             –<a href="/wiki/User:LPfi" title="User:LPfi">LPfi</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:LPfi" title="User talk:LPfi"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 06:12, 21 May 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>
           </dl></li>
         </ul></li>
       </ul> 
       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_19">May 19</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: May 19">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Font_size">Font size</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Font size">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <div style="float: right;">
        <s>{{phab|T283199}}</s>
       </div> 
       <div role="note" style="float:right; clear:right; border:1px solid #999; border-radius:0.5em; background-color:#eee; background-image:linear-gradient(to bottom, #ddd,#eee); font-size:85%; text-align:center; padding:0.5em; margin-left:1em; margin-bottom:1em; width:12em; color: black;" class="plainlinks mw-trackedTemplate">

       </div> 
       <div class="thumb tright">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png" class="image"><img alt="Font size problem Davey2010 1952021.png" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png/220px-Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png/330px-Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png/440px-Font_size_problem_Davey2010_1952021.png 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="697"></a>

       </div> 
       <p>Hi, For some bizarre reason everything on Commons (watchlist, talkpages, upload page) are now in a reduced font size - my page zoom is 100% and Chrome font size is set to "medium (reccommended)" so there doesn't appear to be anything wrong my end? - Wasn't sure if this was WMFs error or Chromes&nbsp;?, Thanks, –<a href="/wiki/User:Davey2010" title="User:Davey2010"><span style="color:blue;"><b>Davey</b></span><span style="color:orange;"><b>2010</b></span></a><sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Davey2010" title="User talk:Davey2010"><span style="color:navy;"><b>Talk</b></span></a></sup> 13:42, 19 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

        </dd> 
        <dd>

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_20">May 20</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: May 20">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Voting_icons">Voting icons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Voting icons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>Currently, most voting templates use <a href="/wiki/Category:Norro_style_1_icons" title="Category:Norro style 1 icons">Norro style 1 icons</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Template:Comment" title="Template:Comment"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Comment}}</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Template:Info" title="Template:Info"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Info}}</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Template:Request" title="Template:Request"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Request}}</span></a>, <a href="/wiki/Template:Question" title="Template:Question"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Question}}</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/Template:Withdraw" title="Template:Withdraw"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Withdraw}}</span></a> use <a href="/wiki/Category:Norro_style_2_icons" title="Category:Norro style 2 icons">Norro style 2 icons</a>. I think we should stick to one set. --<a href="/wiki/User:YavBav09" title="User:YavBav09"><span style="text-shadow:0px 0px 6px #73D216;color:#73D216;">YavBav09</span></a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:YavBav09" title="User talk:YavBav09"><img alt="Icons-mini-comment yellow.gif" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5a/Icons-mini-comment_yellow.gif" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" data-file-width="16" data-file-height="16"></a><a href="/wiki/User_talk:YavBav09" title="User talk:YavBav09"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>)<img alt="Face-smile.svg" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Face-smile.svg/20px-Face-smile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Face-smile.svg/30px-Face-smile.svg.png 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Face-smile.svg/40px-Face-smile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48"> 14:37, 20 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

       <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comments">Comments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Comments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
       <ul>
        <li>While I think that overal Norro Style 2 (two) looks a lot better (graphically), I don't like the fact that the colours a lot softer. In the current version the colours are very strong and bright which makes them stand out better, but the designs of the alternative are superior in almost every other way. So I am currently refraining from voting until I've seen better arguments for or against. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?)        <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_25">May 25</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: May 25">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span id="How_to_search_for_categories.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_search_for_categories?">How to search for categories?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: How to search for categories?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>It used to be quite simple. </p> 
       <ul>
        <li>type word in search .. click on the category search link, click on the category</li>
       </ul> 
       <p>Now it seems impossible: </p> 
       <ul>
        <li>search ends in media search</li> 
        <li>the tab for pages and categories shows galleries</li> 
        <li>the complicated namespace selectors doesn't even allow selecting categories</li>
       </ul> 
       <p>I guess somehow I missed a step to not get there with two words and three simple clicks. Which is it? Search was "Guam village". --- <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jura1" title="User talk:Jura1">Jura1 (talk)</a> 12:47, 25 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         Enter "Category:Guam village" into the search box or select the "old" Special:Search in your user preferences. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Discostu" title="User:Discostu">Discostu</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Discostu" title="User talk:Discostu"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 12:48, 25 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           Interesting. Why would it only show categories in the category tab when typing "Category:"?
          </dd> 
          <dd>
           Maybe there should be a separate "Category" tab that doesn't rely on special user input.
          </dd> 
          <dd>
           User preferences isn't really an option as it requires to be logged in. --- <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jura1" title="User talk:Jura1">Jura1 (talk)</a> 12:57, 25 May 2021 (UTC) 
           <dl>
            <dd>
             What I meant is that you can best search for categories by typing "Category:Guam village" into the search box on any page. It will directly lead you to the "categories and pages" section and give appropriate search results (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nx4332.your-storageshare.de/s/nXsoW4ktRb32esB">Screenshot </a>. If the entered category exists, it will be shown directly in search suggestions and will also be opened directly when pressing enter. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Discostu" title="User:Discostu">Discostu</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Discostu" title="User talk:Discostu"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 13:14, 25 May 2021 (UTC)

              <dd>

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_28">May 28</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: May 28">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span id="The_problem_of_whether_Traditional_Chinese_characters_in_File:Chineselanguage.svg.2C_File:Han-ji.svg.2C_File:Hanzi.svg.2C_File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg_should_use_.22inherited_glyphs_form.22_or_.22standardized_glyphs_form.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_problem_of_whether_Traditional_Chinese_characters_in_File:Chineselanguage.svg,_File:Han-ji.svg,_File:Hanzi.svg,_File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg_should_use_&quot;inherited_glyphs_form&quot;_or_&quot;standardized_glyphs_form&quot;">The problem of whether Traditional Chinese characters in <a href="/wiki/File:Chineselanguage.svg" title="File:Chineselanguage.svg">File:Chineselanguage.svg</a>, <a href="/wiki/File:Han-ji.svg" title="File:Han-ji.svg">File:Han-ji.svg</a>, <a href="/wiki/File:Hanzi.svg" title="File:Hanzi.svg">File:Hanzi.svg</a>, <a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg" title="File:Chinese characters logo.svg">File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg</a> should use "inherited glyphs form" or "standardized glyphs form"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: The problem of whether Traditional Chinese characters in File:Chineselanguage.svg, File:Han-ji.svg, File:Hanzi.svg, File:Chinese characters logo.svg should use &quot;inherited glyphs form&quot; or &quot;standardized glyphs form&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>The latest version of the above image, contributed by Cangjie6, It has already impact on multiple language versions of Wikipedia. In the image, some character use short "?"(?/S/Vertical?form on the radicals like ? and ? ?this form is call "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiu_zixing" class="extiw" title="en:Jiu zixing">Jiu zixing</a>"(Simplified chinese:???; Traditional Chinese:???; pinyin: jiù zìxíng; lit. Old character form) or "inherited glyphs form"(Simplified chinese:????;Traditional Chinese:????; pinyin: chuánchéng zìxíng), which can be found in the Chinese dictionaries before the standardized form of Chinese characters like "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kangxi_Dictionary" class="extiw" title="en:Kangxi Dictionary">Kangxi Dictionary</a>" and the "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhonghua_Da_Zidian" class="extiw" title="en:Zhonghua Da Zidian">Zhonghua Da Zidian</a>", but in the existing standardized form of Chinese characters(listed at the end of) all use "?"(?/D/Dot). </p>
       <p>Note: In File:Hanzi.svg, the simplified chinese part is still written with "?", so this discussion is basically for traditional Chinese characters only. (but still provide the standardized of Simplified Chinese) </p>
       <p><br> I have asked Cangjie6 in zhwiki, and his explanation can be summarized as "inherited glyphs form are more commonly used". </p>
       <p><br>Personally, I propose the following solutions. </p> 
       <ol>
        <li>the most direct, is to go back to the previous version</li> 
        <li>contrary to 1, explore whether the "inherited glyphs form" are more commonly used, or give other reasons for their retention, with reliable sources.</li> 
        <li>A compromise would be to subdivide "traditional Chinese characters" into "nherited glyphs form" and "standardized glyphs form" and show the three variants in the needed image. The premise is that there are reliable sources that prove that both "traditional Chinese characters" have similar weight in most areas where traditional Chinese characters are used.</li>
       </ol> 
       <p><br> Have informed Cangjie6. </p>
       <p><br> Reference documents of standardized: </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <ul>
          <li>Republic of China(Chinese Taipei)??Standard Form of National Characters/??????(aka. A Table/??)?</li>
         </ul> 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <ul>
            <li>“?” 101743 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/SUNGTI/as16.htm">?/Ming/Song</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/fangti/af16.htm">?/Gothic</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/MU/mua16.htm">?/Regular</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/LISHU/as16.htm">?/Clerical</a> (from Offical website)</li> 
            <li>“?” 100987 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/SUNGTI/as9.htm">?/Ming/Song</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/fangti/af9.htm">?/Gothic</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/MU/mua9.htm">?/Regular</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://language.moe.gov.tw/001/Upload/files/SITE_CONTENT/M0001/LISHU/as9.htm">?/Clerical</a> (form Offical website)</li>

             <dl>
              <dd>
               His exact words were: "It was chosen since I made the Cangjie Input Method character example chart and changed it from png pattern to svg pattern when I referred to some glyphs and feedback from input method forums, communication groups, etc. Traditional glyphs have a longer history and are common in modern times, and are more often used in printing, typesetting, cartography, screen display, etc. does not depend only on the Taiwanese and Hong Kong educational glyphs (meaning standardized glyphs), and the Taiwanese and Hong Kong educational glyphs are not specified for uses other than teaching writing."(In fact, Chinese Taipei also requires the use of standardized glyph forms for Government Official Documents)

                <dd>
                 I do not know Chinese. Is the short form versus long form distinction just a font style choice? Some fonts draw a feature one way while other fonts draw it another? For example, a Latin font may or may not have serifs; if the font has serifs, then are the serifs going to be old style, transitional, modern, or slab? The choice is more personal preference and not some semi-official requirement that characters must be drawn a certain way. It is not like English users stopped using the long s: we write "Congress" instead of "Congre?s". I see this issue as a personal preference for particular fonts. 
                 <ul>
                  <li><a href="/wiki/File:Chineselanguage.svg" title="File:Chineselanguage.svg">File:Chineselanguage.svg</a> I would revert this file to the 2018 version. Cangjie6 changed the font to his preference, converted the font to curves, and added colorization. The first two are unnecessary; the colorization is useful to show the character association and could be reapplied.</li> 
                  <li><a href="/wiki/File:Han-ji.svg" title="File:Han-ji.svg">File:Han-ji.svg</a> This file was created by Cangjie6. Its appearance is entirely Cangjie6 choice.</li> 
                  <li><a href="/wiki/File:Hanzi.svg" title="File:Hanzi.svg">File:Hanzi.svg</a> I would revert this file to the 2016 version. Cangjie6 changed the appearance of ? by drawing it in two different fonts. The purpose of this file appears to be that traditional and simplified Chinese draw some characters differently (?/?) but draw other characters the same (?/?). Changing the appearance of the similar character only confuses the issue. The original upload for this file points to the 2006 <a href="/wiki/File:Hanzilead.png" title="File:Hanzilead.png">File:Hanzilead.png</a> which used the same appearance for the similar character.</li> 
                  <li><a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg" title="File:Chinese characters logo.svg">File:Chinese_characters_logo.svg</a> I'd leave this file as is. The image is primarily art. I do not think it needed to be changed, but the red-outlined characters have been improved: they have a cleaner (less jerky) vectorization.</li>
                 </ul>
                </dd> 
                <dd>
                 These are problems that should be on the file pages rather than here. Even if the short/long form distinction is more significant than a font preference, I do not see Commons imposing a requirement that all files must use one of those forms.
                </dd>

       <p><span class="outdent-template" style="font-family:DejaVu Sans, sans-serif; color:#6EC1FC">??????????????????<br></span>It is not only the font that is the problem, although it is more prominent in specific fonts style(?/Regular and ?/Clerica, two fonts style that mimic traditional Chinese calligraphy, the one in the image is ?/Regular) .This involves some basic knowledge of Chinese characters. </p>
       <p>Chinese characters have eight different Basic strokes, which are arranged and combined to form 37 Compound strokes, and 37 Compound strokes are then arranged and combined to form all Chinese characters. You can find a detailed explanation in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroke_(CJK_character)" class="extiw" title="en:Stroke (CJK character)">this Wikipedia article</a>. </p>
       <p>The standardization of Chinese characters suggests, all Chinese characters should use a specific combination of strokes, although some combinations of strokes may look similar, but the standardization suggests that they be treated as different characters. In the "standard reference documents" I gave above for different regions(You can check the specific Chinese characters according to the number. Hong Kong's standards are not numbered and can only be found slowly on specific pages. I have already given the number and page number of "?" and "?" ), it is suggested that the top of "?" and "?" should be "? "(?/D/Dot), but in the image, The tops of "?" and "?" are "?"(?/S/Vertical, it is shorter than in normal writing, so that the difference is not immediately noticeable). This was indeed the customary usage until 1965, when the printed form of Chinese characters was first standardized, as can be seen in the Kangxi Dictionary (published in 1716). Cangjie6 claims that this usage is still common today, so the change was made. </p>
       <p>Because the English name for "Traditional Chinese" says it is "traditional"(In Chinese we say it "cumbersome" or "complex"), you may be confused by the difference. Traditional Chinese is not really traditional, it is just closer to traditional than Simplified Chinese. </p>
       <p>I prefer to follow standardization rather than customary usage, because customary usage is hard to verify, while standardization has authoritative reference documents. But Cangjie6 and others may have a different opinion.translation by Deepl translator--<a href="/wiki/User_talk:%E9%A2%A8%E7%B4%80%E8%82%A1%E9%95%B7" title="User talk:????">???????????????????</a> 00:35, 30 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <ul>
          <li>I did not notice that the CJK Strokes have formal English names before, my input method allows direct output of individual CJK Strokes, so I did it this way, this may not be good. I now add the Chinese name, English name and Unicode name notes.--<a href="/wiki/User_talk:%E9%A2%A8%E7%B4%80%E8%82%A1%E9%95%B7" title="User talk:????">???????????????????</a> 03:17, 30 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_30">May 30</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: May 30">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span id="When_is_a_photo_out_of_scope_because_of_being_a_.22holiday_snap.22.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="When_is_a_photo_out_of_scope_because_of_being_a_&quot;holiday_snap&quot;?">When is a photo out of scope because of being a "holiday snap"?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: When is a photo out of scope because of being a &quot;holiday snap&quot;?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>I nominated several photos of Kasteel Hoensbroek for deletion because a tourist was posing on them, while there were similar photos whithout the tourist. But none of the deletion requests was honored. <br> One of the examples on the Commons page about the project scope explicitly states that "holiday snaps" "are not realistically useful for an educational purpose" and therefor out of scope, see <a href="/wiki/Commons:Project_scope/en#Examples" title="Commons:Project scope/en">Commons:Project scope#Examples</a>. For me these photos clearly are holiday snaps, but apparently other people think differently. Can someone explain to me why these photos are not holiday snaps? (perhaps @<a href="/wiki/User:Missvain" title="User:Missvain">Missvain</a>: who kept these photos?) And what is the definition of a holiday snap? When/in which cases are photos indeed holiday snaps and when not? <br> See: </p> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(11)_(30324098098).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (11) (30324098098).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (11) (30324098098).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(18)_(42383500400).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (18) (42383500400).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (18) (42383500400).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(20)_(42383499620).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (20) (42383499620).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (20) (42383499620).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(22)_(42383498750).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (22) (42383498750).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (22) (42383498750).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(26)_(42383497440).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (26) (42383497440).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (26) (42383497440).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(27)_(43285361165).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (27) (43285361165).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (27) (43285361165).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(41)_(44143064732).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (41) (44143064732).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (41) (44143064732).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(42)_(44143064092).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (42) (44143064092).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (42) (44143064092).jpg</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:Kasteel_Hoensbroek_(45)_(42383492990).jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (45) (42383492990).jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:Kasteel Hoensbroek (45) (42383492990).jpg</a></li>
       </ul> 
       <p><a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JopkeB" title="User talk:JopkeB"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 05:24, 30 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         Personally I am inclined to see a small number of such images on Wikimedia Commons, it would be odd to have a lot of pictures of tourist destinations but never any tourists. On Wikimedia Commons we have a culture that wants pictures without any humans in them as much as possible, but I would argue that how tourists interact with "a tourist magnet" has educational value. Honestly, I would want to know how tourists from the 1930's interacted with colonial tourist spots, but unfortunately very few of such images have been made available online. The term "holiday snaps" is deliberately vague. In fact those are the type of photographs we do want to have, as people tend to go to interesting places, it would be better than people only staying in their local village and only uploading photographs from there. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?) (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/nl:Gebruiker:Donald_Trung/Mijn_werk_%F0%9F%8F%A2" class="extiw" title="w:nl:Gebruiker:Donald Trung/Mijn werk ?">Articles ?</a>)</small> 09:15, 30 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           I agree with Donald. I've sometimes taken similar images of tourists I don't even know for this sort of reason.
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>

       <p>The problem is with images that are mainly a picture of the non-notable person, and where the background is more or less incidental to the photo. - <a href="/wiki/User:Jmabel" title="User:Jmabel">Jmabel</a>&nbsp;! <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jmabel" title="User talk:Jmabel">talk</a> 15:24, 30 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <dl>
            <dd>
             I think the idea behind the holiday snap rule is to avoid posed photographs where the people in the picture are not even acting naturally, rather posing for the photograph with the purpose of showing it to family and friends, Therefore making it only of interest to the people involved. <a href="/wiki/User:Oxyman" title="User:Oxyman">Oxyman</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Oxyman" title="User talk:Oxyman"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 16:07, 30 May 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         I interpret the "holiday snaps" line to refer not to photos of a posing non-notable individual, but to photos that don't usefully depict anything other than such an individual. Even with photos of the second type, I don't bother bogging down the DR process with them: if there are enough useful photos of the subject <i>without</i> people in them I just dump the people ones in a subcategory such as <a href="/wiki/Category:People_in_Bryce_Canyon_National_Park" title="Category:People in Bryce Canyon National Park">Category:People in Bryce Canyon National Park</a>. That keeps them out of the way of people who aren't looking for them specifically, which is really the only reason we would delete them, IMO. – <a href="/wiki/User:BMacZero" title="User:BMacZero">BMacZero</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:BMacZero#top" title="User talk:BMacZero">?</a>) 16:36, 30 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           For the Taj Mahal there is a category <a href="/wiki/Category:Visitors_of_the_Taj_Mahal" title="Category:Visitors of the Taj Mahal">Visitors of the Taj Mahal</a> with images such as <a href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_and_grounds_Dalans_round_Taj_Quadrangle..JPG" title="File:Taj Mahal and grounds Dalans round Taj Quadrangle..JPG">this one</a> and <a href="/wiki/File:Sally_and_Dave_non-selfie_(13174967924).jpg" title="File:Sally and Dave non-selfie (13174967924).jpg">that one</a>. I agree with Donald Trung that how tourists interact with "a tourist magnet" can have educational value. <a href="/wiki/User:Wouterhagens" title="User:Wouterhagens">Wouter</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wouterhagens" title="User talk:Wouterhagens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 19:01, 30 May 2021 (UTC)
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <ul>
        <li>It isn't. Ever. It's out of scope because it <i>doesn't</i> meet <a href="/wiki/Commons:SCOPE" class="mw-redirect" title="Commons:SCOPE">COM:SCOPE</a>, i.e. there is a <i>lack</i> of reasons why it could potentially be within scope. But being something else as well, such as a "holiday snap", "personal photo", "selfie" or whatever doesn't <i>remove</i> it from scope. Many things are both holiday snaps <i>and</i> valued images within scope - particularly if they're older and of a location where there would be few holiday snaps otherwise.</li>
       </ul> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         On the other hand, a holiday snap of Ibiza, Cancun or the Pyramids of Giza might find it <i>hard</i> to pass SCOPE, as there are already a surfeit of images from that place and time. But it's not ruled out. <a href="/wiki/User:Andy_Dingley" title="User:Andy Dingley">Andy Dingley</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Andy_Dingley" title="User talk:Andy Dingley"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 20:04, 30 May 2021 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <ul>
        <li>The only time I really object is when the same person is in hundreds of images, grinning into the camera. It feels like that person is engaging in self promotion. <a href="/wiki/User:Krok6kola" title="User:Krok6kola">Krok6kola</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Krok6kola" title="User talk:Krok6kola"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 20:18, 30 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
       </ul> 
       <ul>
        <li>Thanks for all your reactions; this is beyond my expectations. So now this discussion is about multiple questions:</li>
       </ul> 
       <ol>
        <li>Would it be good to have some photos of tourists at tourist destinations, about how humans interact with tourist magnets?</li> 
        <li>If yes: what kind of photos should that be? Should they be only taken of non posing people, only of people who are acting naturally? For instance: people waiting in a line, having fun, taking pictures, looking at objects in a museum, and so on.</li> 
        <li>Are photos with posing non-notable people OK? Or only if there are no similar photos of the subject without people? Or certainly not when the same person is in many images, grinning into the camera?</li> 
        <li>Should the Project scope be adjusted, or only the example with the "holiday snaps"? Should "holiday snaps" be defined here?</li> 
        <li>Was it right that the photos of Kasteel Hoensbroek which had a deletion request were kept?</li>
       </ol> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         My personal answers:
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <ol>
        <li>Yes, I agree. Otherwise there would be a gap in an important way people spend their holidays. It would be odd to have only photos of beaches, Disneyland, the Eiffel Tour, museums and so on without people. These images should be in a category like <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:People_at_visitor_attractions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:People at visitor attractions (page does not exist)">Category: People at visitor attractions</a> and it's subcategories.</li> 
        <li>Yes: those photos should only be taken of non posing people, only of people who are acting naturally, like the second photo of Oxyman, from Sibiu. I have no problems with these kind of photos at all.</li> 
        <li>No, photos with posing non-notable people are not OK. Certainly not when the same person is in many images, grinning into the camera. For me "many" is already three, not hundred. I think self promotion is certainly not within the scope of this project. Perhaps an exception can be made if there are no similar photos of the subject without people or if they wear typical clothes, characteristic for a certain period or area of which are few or none other images in Commons.</li> 
        <li>"Holiday snaps" should be defined on the Project scope page.</li> 
        <li>No, I don't think so, otherwise I would not have nominated them for deletion. The same person was posing on the first six of the photos while there were similar photos without a posing person. Another person was posing on the three others, taking pictures of himself in the mirror.</li>
       </ol>

       <h2><span id="What_is_the_English_word_for_.22meterkast.22_.28Dutch.29.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="What_is_the_English_word_for_&quot;meterkast&quot;_(Dutch)?">What is the English word for "meterkast" (Dutch)?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: What is the English word for &quot;meterkast&quot; (Dutch)?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <div class="thumb tright">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Meterkast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Meterkast.jpg/220px-Meterkast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="382" class="thumbimage" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Meterkast.jpg/330px-Meterkast.jpg 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Meterkast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="378" data-file-height="657"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Meterkast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>Meterkast - what is it in English?
         </div>
        </div>
       </div> 
       <p>In the Netherlands every house and building has a "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/nl:Meterkast" class="extiw" title="w:nl:Meterkast">meterkast</a>", a small closet in which gas, electric and water flow into the building; for each of these here are flow meters. From there gas, electric and water flow through pipes into the house/building. Here are also the main taps, in case of an emergency or reparations to shut down gas or water for the whole building. I assume that other countries have similar closets, but I cannot find a proper category, nor a proper English word. My questions: </p> 
       <ol>
        <li>Is there already a category for these <i>meterkasten</i>?</li> 
        <li>If not, what is the English word? <a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q3018179" class="extiw" title="d:Q3018179">Wikidata</a> does not give a translation. Google Translate gives 'fuse box', but that is only a part of a meterkast.</li>
       </ol> 
       <p><a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JopkeB" title="User talk:JopkeB"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 07:39, 30 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a> We have <a href="/wiki/Category:Gas_meters" title="Category:Gas meters">Category:Gas meters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Water_meters" title="Category:Water meters">Category:Water meters</a> for example but not a category for the box/closet/room they are in. --<a href="/wiki/User:MGA73" title="User:MGA73">MGA73</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:MGA73" title="User talk:MGA73"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 09:37, 30 May 2021 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <ul>
        <li>(UK) "Meter box" for the sort over the last 30 years, built into an outside wall. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.meterboxesdirect.co.uk/electric-meter-box.html">https://www.meterboxesdirect.co.uk/electric-meter-box.html</a> "Meter cupboard" if they're older and internal. For fairly obvious reasons, the outdoor-acccessible ones don't contain the fuse box. <a href="/wiki/User:Andy_Dingley" title="User:Andy Dingley">Andy Dingley</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Andy_Dingley" title="User talk:Andy Dingley"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 09:41, 30 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
       </ul> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           I like the question: this could off course be a completely Dutch efficiency thing.&nbsp;:)
          </dd> 
          <dd>
           Interglot gives "meter cupboard", but there no English article by that name. German translation on Interglot gives no hits, but they for sure use a closet for their collection of in-house meters as well. <a href="/wiki/User:Ciell" title="User:Ciell">Ciell</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Ciell" title="User talk:Ciell"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:48, 30 May 2021 (UTC) 
           <ul>
            <li>Note also that UK practice doesn't run water through here. Water meters in the UK are still in the minority, except for new-build estates. Our water supply enters separately, finds its own route through the house (often a mystery to householder and plumbers alike) and not having a meter, has no great urge to share an accessible meter box. <a href="/wiki/User:Andy_Dingley" title="User:Andy Dingley">Andy Dingley</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Andy_Dingley" title="User talk:Andy Dingley"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 20:09, 30 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
           </ul>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <p>Thank you all for your answers. </p> 
       <ol>
        <li>I conclude that the correct name would be <a href="/wiki/Category:Meter_cupboards" title="Category:Meter cupboards">Category:Meter cupboards</a> for indoor "Meterkasten" and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:Meter_boxes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:Meter boxes (page does not exist)">Category:Meter boxes</a> for boxes outside. Is it correct that a parent category for Category:Meter cupboards would be <a href="/wiki/Category:Cupboards" title="Category:Cupboards">Category:Cupboards</a>? (For me it would be more logical to have <a href="/wiki/Category:Rooms" title="Category:Rooms">Category:Rooms</a> or <a href="/wiki/Category:Closets" title="Category:Closets">Category:Closets</a> to be the parent category because it is about a room with a door; a cupboard is often thought of as a movable thing.)<br></li> 
        <li>And I conclude that my assumption that other countries have similar closets, is not true: there may be other solutions.<br></li> 
        <li>@<a href="/wiki/User:Ciell" title="User:Ciell">Ciell</a>: It might not only be an efficiency thing but also be obliged by law.</li>
       </ol> 
       <p><a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JopkeB" title="User talk:JopkeB"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 07:06, 31 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         @<a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a>: From my experience, <a href="/wiki/Category:Meter_cupboards" title="Category:Meter cupboards">Category:Meter cupboards</a> for indoor "Meterkasten" and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:Meter_boxes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:Meter boxes (page does not exist)">Category:Meter boxes</a> for boxes outside is fine (although <a href="/wiki/Category:Meter_cupboards" title="Category:Meter cupboards">Category:Meter cupboards</a> is somewhat unamerican, perhaps the more direct translation <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:Meter_closets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:Meter closets (page does not exist)">Category:Meter closets</a>), but larger ones could also be called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:Meter_rooms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:Meter rooms (page does not exist)">Category:Meter rooms</a> or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Category:Utility_rooms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Category:Utility rooms (page does not exist)">Category:Utility rooms</a> (convenient places I have seen contain water heaters, alarm systems, HVAC systems, water sprinkler systems, and demarcation points for phone &amp; cable, as well as the occasional extra freezer). &nbsp; — <span style="font-size:115%;background:#FFA"><a href="/wiki/User:Jeff_G." title="User:Jeff G.">Jeff G.</a></span> ?<small><sub> please <a href="/wiki/Template:Ping" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Ping">ping</a> or <a href="/wiki/User:Jeff_G./talk" class="mw-redirect" title="User:Jeff G./talk">talk to me</a></sub></small> 14:39, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           A significant difference - UK at least - is that "meter boxes" are publicly accessible. Or at least, accessible to meter readers, who don't need the occupant's permission (or presence) to let them access the box and read the meter. So this box is also limited as to what's in it - there's no easy way to shut off the supply, or to abstract electricity from someone else's account (It can be and is done, but it's theft and leaves traces). So a meter box will still often have a meter cupboard indoors too, with no meter, but the fusebox. <a href="/wiki/User:Andy_Dingley" title="User:Andy Dingley">Andy Dingley</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Andy_Dingley" title="User talk:Andy Dingley"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 21:16, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
           <dl>
            <dd>
             @<a href="/wiki/User:Jeff_G." title="User:Jeff G.">Jeff G.</a>: there might be a reason why the Dutch don't like to mix electricity and water though :p. Every house has a separate boiler room, except for very old buildings maybe, where these are just below the sink/in the attic/etc.
            </dd> 
            <dd>
             @<a href="/wiki/User:JopkeB" title="User:JopkeB">JopkeB</a>: Yes, indeed we have regulations to have these at the front door! Must be for safety, right?
            </dd> 
            <dd>
             @<a href="/wiki/User:Andy_Dingley" title="User:Andy Dingley">Andy Dingley</a>: recently most of us received 'smart meters' that just automatically sign through your numbers, but "back in the day" they would just charge you for an estimated amount if you did not fill out in the form they would send you every year, or let the meter-men in. My previous flat did have a central water meter, but that is an exception over here. This is where we can also find the fuses for our personal apartment, and this is where internet/tv/telephone/fiber enters your apartment as well. <a href="/wiki/User:Ciell" title="User:Ciell">Ciell</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Ciell" title="User talk:Ciell"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 21:48, 2 June 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Request_to_help_save_valuable_images_of_identity_documents">Request to help save valuable images of identity documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Request to help save valuable images of identity documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>I am quite busy with a lot of things and therefore don't have the time to invest in this, but at "<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Huddyhuddy#Source_of_derivative_work_is_not_properly_indicated:_File:0passport_1951.jpg" title="User talk:Huddyhuddy">User talk:Huddyhuddy#Source of derivative work is not properly indicated: File:0passport 1951.jpg</a>" there is a large list of old identity documents being tagged for automated deletion because of improper sourcing and licensing. Most of these files are quite clearly in the public domain, for example at "<a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/File:1914_Turkish_Ottoman_passport_issued_at_Jaffa.jpg" title="Commons:Deletion requests/File:1914 Turkish Ottoman passport issued at Jaffa.jpg">Commons:Deletion requests/File:1914 Turkish Ottoman passport issued at Jaffa.jpg</a>" I noted that the file already had a description that looked like this: </p> 
       <div class="hproduct commons-file-information-table"> 
        <table class="fileinfotpl-type-information toccolours vevent mw-content-ltr" style="width: 100%; direction: ltr;" cellpadding="4"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="vertical-align: top"> 
           <td id="fileinfotpl_desc" class="fileinfo-paramfield" lang="en">Description<span class="summary fn" style="display:none">Village pump</span></td> 
           <td class="description"> 
            <div class="description mw-content-ltr en" dir="ltr" lang="en">
             <span class="language en" title="English"><b>English: </b></span> 1914 Turkish Ottoman passport issued at Jaffa.
            </div></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr style="vertical-align: top"> 
           <td id="fileinfotpl_date" class="fileinfo-paramfield" lang="en">Date</td> 
           <td lang="en"> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><time class="dtstart" datetime="1914">1914</time></span></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr style="vertical-align: top"> 
           <td id="fileinfotpl_src" class="fileinfo-paramfield" lang="en">Source</td> 
           <td> Huddyhuddy's passport collection</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr style="vertical-align: top"> 
           <td id="fileinfotpl_aut" class="fileinfo-paramfield" lang="en">Author</td> 
           <td> Government of the Ottoman Empire</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr style="vertical-align: top"> 
           <td id="fileinfotpl_perm" class="fileinfo-paramfield" lang="en">Permission<br><small>(<a href="/wiki/Commons:Reusing_content_outside_Wikimedia" title="Commons:Reusing content outside Wikimedia">Reusing this file</a>)</small></td> 
           <td> <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-Ottoman" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:PD-Ottoman"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{PD-Ottoman}}</span></a></td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
       <p>(DON'T ADD COPYRIGHT © AND SOURCE TAGS LIKE THIS, THIS IS DEEMED INSUFFICIENT.) </p>
       <p>But this is seemed insufficient by Commonswiki sysops, so these files need more editing. Furthermore, some of the files tagged for deletion are a French passport from 1800 and a United States passport from 1815. These files simply need to have their copyright © tags replaced and sources listed, at least I thought so until I saw the Ottoman passport listed for deletion, so I have no idea how to fix them. Because of my lack of time I would like for other volunteers to invest their time to save these files which have very high educational, cultural, and historical value. </p>
       <p>Also, please just nominate each individual file for deletion to let enough volunteers judge them individually. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?) (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/nl:Gebruiker:Donald_Trung/Mijn_werk_%F0%9F%8F%A2" class="extiw" title="w:nl:Gebruiker:Donald Trung/Mijn werk ?">Articles ?</a>)</small> 08:36, 30 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <ul>
        <li>?n example of how to fix these could be found at "<a href="/wiki/File:Sugihara_visa.jpg" title="File:Sugihara visa.jpg">File:Sugihara visa.jpg</a>". Apparently the Creative Commons licenses have to be completely removed, simply adding license tags that the underlying image is in the public domain will still get them deleted. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?)        <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="May_31">May 31</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: May 31">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Categorizing_uncategorized_images">Categorizing uncategorized images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Categorizing uncategorized images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>I have been spending a lot of time recently categorizing uncategorized images uploaded by DPLA bot, but am I wasting my time? Is there a bot that will categorize these images? I note that when I upload a photo usually a bunch of (often superfluous) categories get added to it. <a href="/wiki/User:Mztourist" title="User:Mztourist">Mztourist</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Mztourist" title="User talk:Mztourist"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:06, 31 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         I think it depends on the kind of images and on the kind of categories you are adding. But my general experience with uploads by DLPA bots is that they are just dumped into Commons and then left here without useful categories. So what you are doing is valuable work (but an uphill battle). -- <a href="/wiki/User:Discostu" title="User:Discostu">Discostu</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Discostu" title="User talk:Discostu"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:40, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           Thanks <a href="/wiki/User:Discostu" title="User:Discostu">Discostu</a> good to know its not a waste of time, but feels Sisyphusian! <a href="/wiki/User:Mztourist" title="User:Mztourist">Mztourist</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Mztourist" title="User talk:Mztourist"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 11:01, 31 May 2021 (UTC)
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <ul>
            <li>@<a href="/wiki/User:Mztourist" title="User:Mztourist">Mztourist</a>: It’s not a waste of time, and thank you for your effort! -- <a href="/wiki/User:Tuvalkin" title="User:Tuvalkin">Tuválkin</a> <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Tuvalkin" title="User talk:Tuvalkin">?</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin" title="Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin">?</a> 03:55, 1 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
           </ul>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <p>Someone pointed out this thread to me. DPLA uploads are currently only categorized by source institution on upload. There are no real topical categories we can add programmatically based on the data, especially when working at the scale of millions of files, since manually inspecting each upload would create a bottleneck. That is how it was ever since the bot was approved, but I think the <a href="/wiki/Template:Uncategorized" title="Template:Uncategorized">{{Uncategorized}}</a> only recently started being added to these. (It's being added by another bot, and I don't necessarily mind either way if the community wants to consider these "Uncategorized", depending on what you your needs are.) The goal here is not to dump these on the Commons community or create work for others, though. We are currently actively planning further development of the bot to improve synchronization, so we can iterate on the data over time and add SDC statements. If you have any suggestion on how we can improve the format of the automated uploads, I'm certainly open to making improvements. <a href="/wiki/User:Dominic" title="User:Dominic">Dominic</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Dominic" title="User talk:Dominic"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 18:19, 3 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <h2><span id="Possible_bug_with_Wikidata:Suggestededit-add.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_bug_with_Wikidata:Suggestededit-add?">Possible bug with Wikidata:Suggestededit-add?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Possible bug with Wikidata:Suggestededit-add?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <dl>
        <dt>
         <a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Wikidata:Suggestededit-add_1.0" class="extiw" title="d:Wikidata:Suggestededit-add 1.0">Wikidata:Suggestededit-add 1.0</a>
        </dt>
       </dl> 
       <p>In the light of the SuggestedTags bug <a href="https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/T283431" class="extiw" title="phab:T283431">phab:T283431</a>, which results in pseudo random tags being added as the first in a list of matches is added rather than the one the user clicked on, is there a way that the contributions from <a class="external text" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Contributions/Hasimfeyyaz&amp;offset=&amp;limit=500&amp;target=Hasimfeyyaz">Hasimfeyyaz</a> can be emulated using Suggestededit that might explain that their attempts to add Turkish Wikidata descriptions could have all been done in good faith? </p>
       <p>Asking because I flagged these edits at ANU and the user's account has been indef blocked based solely on this evidence, but as I have never used Suggestededit myself, this is not something that I considered possible. --<a href="/wiki/User:F%C3%A6" title="User:Fæ">Fæ</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:F%C3%A6" title="User talk:Fæ"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:30, 31 May 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         Commenting as the author of the ticket mentioned above and as a regular user of Suggested Edits:
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         1. I have never encountered any bugs when using Suggested Edits.
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         2. There is no reason to believe that the bug would happen for a certain user and for every of their edits but not for other users.
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         -- <a href="/wiki/User:Discostu" title="User:Discostu">Discostu</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Discostu" title="User talk:Discostu"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:37, 31 May 2021 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <h2><span id="Speedy_deletion_of_dozens_of_images_kept_in_previous_dr.2C_endeletion_requests_by_an_administrator"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Speedy_deletion_of_dozens_of_images_kept_in_previous_dr,_endeletion_requests_by_an_administrator">Speedy deletion of dozens of images kept in previous dr, endeletion requests by an administrator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Speedy deletion of dozens of images kept in previous dr, endeletion requests by an administrator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>Now some uber-users can do what they want and dont follow the rules? One paradigmatic case is the speedy deletion of dozens (if not hundreds or even thousands) of images as being "Self-delete. Unused personal photo. Out of project scope?", by the administrator <a href="/wiki/User:Moheen" title="User:Moheen">User:Moheen</a> when their scope was pretty much estabished in <a href="/wiki/Commons:Deletion_requests/Files_in_Category:Files_from_Lies_Thru_a_Lens_Flickr_stream" title="Commons:Deletion requests/Files in Category:Files from Lies Thru a Lens Flickr stream">Commons:Deletion requests/Files in Category:Files from Lies Thru a Lens Flickr stream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commons:Village_pump/Copyright/Archive/2018/07#Mass_delete_help" title="Commons:Village pump/Copyright/Archive/2018/07">Commons:Village_pump/Copyright</a> and <a class="external text" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=Commons:Undeletion_requests/Current_requests&amp;oldid=338189187#Files_from_Lies_Thru_a_Lens_Flickr_stream">an undeletion request</a> and they are not images taken by this administrator. </p>

          <li>@<a href="/wiki/User:Moheen" title="User:Moheen">Moheen</a>: Undelete all and submit a proper DR, or speedy delete again using this time a recognized speedy deletion rationale. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Tuvalkin" title="User:Tuvalkin">Tuválkin</a> <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Tuvalkin" title="User talk:Tuvalkin">?</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin" title="Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin">?</a> 23:59, 2 June 2021 (UTC)</li>

        <dd>
         I have an overall concern about repeated mass deletions as creating precedent for future actions here on the Commons. Is there any tracking or monitoring of mass deletions at all? Is there a category for files (kept) that have been the target of repeated deletion requests? If not, where do I propose this category creation or can I just do it myself? There could be sub-categories on the number of DR attempts, for instance. Categories would help me and other editors understand more about these actions, which can used to create possible improvement to process or policy. --<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Ooligan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Ooligan (page does not exist)">Ooligan</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Ooligan" title="User talk:Ooligan"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 18:34, 1 June 2021 (UTC)

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="June_01">June 01</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: June 01">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span id="Where_does_the_description_come_from.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Where_does_the_description_come_from?">Where does the description come from?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Where does the description come from?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>In <a href="/wiki/File:Pokharaboats.jpg" title="File:Pokharaboats.jpg">File:Pokharaboats.jpg</a> is the description "English: Boats at fewa lake, Pokhara" including a link as a pencil symbol. I was curious about that symbol. In the edit form I see only "|description=". Where does the desciption come from? <a href="/wiki/User:Wouterhagens" title="User:Wouterhagens">Wouter</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wouterhagens" title="User talk:Wouterhagens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 07:57, 1 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         It may have something to do with the fact that the country code for Nepal (np) is not entered in <a href="/wiki/Template:Wiki_Loves_Earth_2020" title="Template:Wiki Loves Earth 2020"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Wiki Loves Earth 2020}}</span></a>. <a href="/wiki/User:GeorgHH" title="User:GeorgHH">GeorgHH</a> • <small><u><tt><a href="/wiki/User_talk:GeorgHH" title="User talk:GeorgHH">talk</a></tt></u></small>&nbsp;&nbsp; 09:55, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         @<a href="/wiki/User:Wouterhagens" title="User:Wouterhagens">Wouterhagens</a>: It's from the file's caption. I think <a href="/wiki/Template:Information" title="Template:Information"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Information}}</span></a> defaults to using the caption(s) when there's no description. See <a href="/wiki/Commons:File_captions" title="Commons:File captions">Commons:File captions</a> for more about captions. --<a href="/wiki/User:Bjh21" title="User:Bjh21">bjh21</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Bjh21" title="User talk:Bjh21"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:45, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         Yes, the information template was changed to use effectively invisible structured data, because it's not in the wikitext. For a systems change with no clear consensus, it's an amazing extra level of complexity for bot writers, considering that the API changes to cater for this has yet to happen. For my own uploads I only check wikitext, if it stuff is not there, there it does not exist and should be considered unreliable, considering that disruptive caption vandalism is not properly detectable at the current time. Nobody has produced a coherent rationale as to why my own future upload projects should change their wikitext based approach. --<a href="/wiki/User:F%C3%A6" title="User:Fæ">Fæ</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:F%C3%A6" title="User talk:Fæ"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 11:52, 1 June 2021 (UTC) 
         <ul>
          <li>@<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Wouter&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Wouter (page does not exist)">Wouter</a>, <a href="/wiki/User:F%C3%A6" title="User:Fæ">Fæ</a>: It’s a nuisance, but it’s not the worst thing in the war Wikidata is waging on Commons. At least while it can be circumvented by filling the affected <a href="/wiki/Template:Information" title="Template:Information"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Information}}</span></a> field one wants to keep blank with some dummy textual data, such as <code>&amp;nbsp;</code>, unrendered wikitext such as <code>'' ''</code>, or invisible HTML such as <code>&lt;!-- nothing here --&gt;</code>. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Tuvalkin" title="User:Tuvalkin">Tuválkin</a> <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Tuvalkin" title="User talk:Tuvalkin">?</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin" title="Special:Contributions/Tuvalkin">?</a> 23:55, 2 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
         </ul> 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <dl>
            <dd>
             If someone wants to kick off a bot task to fill in "blank" information templates by blindly copying where caption text exists that would be super. Unfortunately, the WMF changed the standard upload wizard without any consensus so that newbies are driven to fill in captions before anything else, without understanding that the priority should be to complete the description field.
            </dd> 
            <dd>
             This does massively increase the marketability of Wikimedia Commons for selling on for Machine Learning, free human faces with tagging/metadata is very commercial desired, but the net benefit to volunteers is purely negative mainly because the changes were never tested and as a result have a crappy workflow and usability problems. Sadly the WMF does not even cash in on the reselling that is already happening, as we see with Getty resellers. --<a href="/wiki/User:F%C3%A6" title="User:Fæ">Fæ</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:F%C3%A6" title="User talk:Fæ"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:48, 3 June 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_file_versions_fails_to_replace_older_one">New file versions fails to replace older one</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: New file versions fails to replace older one">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>Hi Commons community. I uploaded two newer versions of <a href="/wiki/File:Carte_de_l%27Empire_romain_en_118_apr%C3%A8s_J.-C.jpg" title="File:Carte de l'Empire romain en 118 après J.-C.jpg">File:Carte de l'Empire romain en 118 après J.-C.jpg</a>. My last version is displayed atop the file page, but <a class="external text" href="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Carte_de_l%27Empire_romain_en_118_apr%C3%A8s_J.-C.jpg">the zommable picture</a> is still the original version.        <h2><span id="How_do_I_programmatically_request_an_image_properties_.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="How_do_I_programmatically_request_an_image_properties_?">How do I programmatically request an image properties&nbsp;?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: How do I programmatically request an image properties&nbsp;?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>Hope its the good place to ask... </p>
       <p>Image pages contain a lot of information like that one: </p>
       <p><a class="external free" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Lady_with_an_Ermine_-_Leonardo_da_Vinci_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg">https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Lady_with_an_Ermine_-_Leonardo_da_Vinci_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg</a> </p>
       <p>image size, licensing, wikidata link, etc. </p>
       <p>Is it possible to programmatically get that information&nbsp;? An http request returning a JSON is fine. </p>
       <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Laurent.Claessens" title="User talk:Laurent.Claessens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 15:36, 2 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         @<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a>: Please see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://magnus-toolserver.toolforge.org/commonsapi.php">here</a>. This API can programmatically request a lot of info on Commons files. <b style="line-height:1.1;display:inline-block;transform:skew(-14deg);border-radius:2em;border:solid#34c 1px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/User:Mysterymanblue" title="User:Mysterymanblue"><b style="color:#fff;background:#34c">?Mysteryman</b></a><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Mysterymanblue" title="User talk:Mysterymanblue">blue?</a></b> 18:23, 2 June 2021 (UTC)
        </dd> 
        <dd>
         @<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a>: I'd suggest exploring the <a href="/wiki/Special:ApiSandbox" title="Special:ApiSandbox">Special:ApiSandbox</a>. You probably want to start by setting <code>action=query</code> and putting the page title (including the "File:" prefix) in <code>titles</code>. Once you've got the sandbox producing the output you want, you can copy the URL for the query from the result page. --<a href="/wiki/User:Bjh21" title="User:Bjh21">bjh21</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Bjh21" title="User talk:Bjh21"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 18:46, 2 June 2021 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <dl>
          <dd>

Thanks.<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Laurent.Claessens" title="User talk:Laurent.Claessens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 05:26, 3 June 2021 (UTC)

I must be missing something.<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Laurent.Claessens" title="User talk:Laurent.Claessens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 05:26, 3 June 2021 (UTC)
