       <p>In the meantime (mixing the answers and other researches) I found this way to get a JSON containing the information about an image: <a class="external free" href="https://www.mediawiki.org/w/api.php?action=query&amp;prop=imageinfo&amp;iiprop=extmetadata&amp;format=json&amp;titles=File:Leonardo,_Madonna_Benois.JPG">https://www.mediawiki.org/w/api.php?action=query&amp;prop=imageinfo&amp;iiprop=extmetadata&amp;format=json&amp;titles=File:Leonardo,_Madonna_Benois.JPG</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Laurent.Claessens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Laurent.Claessens (page does not exist)">Laurent.Claessens</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Laurent.Claessens" title="User talk:Laurent.Claessens"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 05:26, 3 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Collective_bots">Collective bots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Collective bots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>Wikimedia Commons, in fact all Wikimedia websites, have an odd culture in the way that it is both hyper-individualistic compared to most popular websites, yet is collaborative in every level of its functioning. When you upload your own works to Wikimedia Commons they are <i>your</i> copyright © for as long as you choose them to be, yet any file may be edited by anyone (excluding significant overwrites of copyrighted works). In this environment bots edit almost everything by almost every user, files are given Structured Data on Wikimedia Commons (SDC) metadata through bots, every registered user gets greeted by a bot, and bots even delete some files automatically with minimal human oversight. I would argue that these are all good things (excluding the deletion without review, but humans are at least given the opportunity to fix those). But each and all of these bots are individually operated and individually maintained. </p>
       <p>So I would like to propose that we would allow "Collective bots", these would be bots operated by multiple (trusted) users and any of the current operators of a collective bot could adjust its code for new API's and / or new tasks. Also other (trusted) users could then be given access to a collective bot or become co-operators. </p>
       <p>The limitations on which users should be allowed to operate should be in the hands of the "operating collective" ("operating community") and should preferably only be limited to people with experience running bots on Wikimedia Commons (or perhaps other Wikimedia websites). </p> 
       <dl>
        <dt>
         Examples.
        </dt>
       </dl> 
       <p>We could have a "DepictsBot", "SDC-bot", Etc. operated by multiple people, if one user decides to retire then another user wouldn't have to need to code such a bot from scratch and just take over the bot, if multiple people already operate a bot and one (1) decides to retire (or gets community banned, or dies, or has urgent real life affairs, gives up due to the WMF forcing changes in the software, Etc.) then another user can simply continue operating without much of a hassle. I am not immediately proposing this in the proposals village pump because I first want to hear the arguments for and against this and how to improve. Unless this is already allowed, but I haven't been able to find much on that. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?) (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/nl:Gebruiker:Donald_Trung/Mijn_werk_%F0%9F%8F%A2" class="extiw" title="w:nl:Gebruiker:Donald Trung/Mijn werk ?">Articles ?</a>)</small> 22:19, 2 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         @<a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung</a>: We already have some collective bots and operators of multiple bots, but information about them is scarce. &nbsp; — <span style="font-size:115%;background:#FFA"><a href="/wiki/User:Jeff_G." title="User:Jeff G.">Jeff G.</a></span> ?<small><sub> please <a href="/wiki/Template:Ping" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Ping">ping</a> or <a href="/wiki/User:Jeff_G./talk" class="mw-redirect" title="User:Jeff G./talk">talk to me</a></sub></small> 00:39, 3 June 2021 (UTC) 
         <dl>
          <dd>
           Then the nature of this discussion changed. Then I would like to see clear guidelines for how they work at "<a href="/wiki/Commons:Bots#Collective_bots" title="Commons:Bots">Commons:Bots#Collective bots</a>" or something. Oftentimes things are allowed on Wikimedia websites, but they are "unwritten rules". Most of these websites function like this. --<small><a href="/wiki/User:Donald_Trung" title="User:Donald Trung">Donald Trung ?????</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Donald_Trung" title="User talk:Donald Trung">No Fake News ?</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Commons:WikiProject_Numismatics" title="Commons:WikiProject Numismatics">WikiProject Numismatics</a> ?) (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/nl:Gebruiker:Donald_Trung/Mijn_werk_%F0%9F%8F%A2" class="extiw" title="w:nl:Gebruiker:Donald Trung/Mijn werk ?">Articles ?</a>)</small> 05:57, 3 June 2021 (UTC) 
           <dl>
            <dd>
             See <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Help:Toolforge/Abandoned_tool_policy" class="extiw" title="wikitech:Help:Toolforge/Abandoned tool policy">wikitech:Help:Toolforge/Abandoned tool policy</a> and <a href="https://wikitech.wikimedia.org/wiki/Help:Toolforge/Developing_successful_tools" class="extiw" title="wikitech:Help:Toolforge/Developing successful tools">wikitech:Help:Toolforge/Developing successful tools</a>. Bigger bots often need to span more than one Wikimedia project, so these sorts of policies make more sense to not be just Commons specific. BTW, a LOT of the policies and guidelines are effective recommendations because there is no global police force stopping people from being bold and trying to improve stuff with automated tasks, unless the local project has decided to become authoritarian about it (not Commons). --<a href="/wiki/User:F%C3%A6" title="User:Fæ">Fæ</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:F%C3%A6" title="User talk:Fæ"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 10:55, 3 June 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>

       <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="June_03">June 03</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: June 03">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
       <h2><span id="Video2commons_scrubbing_metadata.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Video2commons_scrubbing_metadata?">Video2commons scrubbing metadata?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Video2commons scrubbing metadata?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>I just uploaded a video of mine using <a href="/wiki/Commons:Video2commons" title="Commons:Video2commons">Video2commons</a> and noticed that it lacked metadata. It's really not great if our in-house tool for video conversion is failing to preserve highly useful information about a video such as when and where it was taken, and this also makes it harder for us to detect copyright violations (as a lack of metadata can be a key indicator that a contribution is not someone's own work). Can we resolve this? <span style="color:#AAA"><small>{{u|</small><span style="border-radius:9em;padding:0 5px;background:#088"><a href="/wiki/User:Sdkb" title="User:Sdkb"><span style="color:#FFF"><b>Sdkb</b></span></a></span><small>}}</small></span>?<sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Sdkb" title="User talk:Sdkb"><b>talk</b></a></sup> 02:06, 3 June 2021 (UTC) </p>

       <h2><span id="Am_I_allowed_to_edit_the_permission_information_of_a_file.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Am_I_allowed_to_edit_the_permission_information_of_a_file?">Am I allowed to edit the permission information of a file?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commons:Village_pump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Am I allowed to edit the permission information of a file?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <p>I would like to use <a class="external text" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:The_Morita-za_formal_curtain.svg">this file</a> in Wikipedia. It has been tagged as an own work of the uploader and been released into the Public domain. But I found that this pattern is a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.shochiku.co.jp/engeki/kabuki-license/a_right/">trademark</a> of an Japanese theater, so it would be better to use <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-shape" title="Template:PD-shape">Template:PD-shape</a> and <a href="/wiki/Template:Trademarked" title="Template:Trademarked">Template:Trademarked</a> rather than the <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-self" title="Template:PD-self">Template:PD-self</a>. However, I have no knowledge of wikimedia, and unsure if I can edit the license directly since I am not the uploader. Any advice would be appreciated.--<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:%E7%AB%8B%E6%97%A5&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:?? (page does not exist)">??</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:%E7%AB%8B%E6%97%A5" title="User talk:??"><span class="signature-talk">talk</span></a>) 14:06, 4 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
       <ul>
        <li>Certainly anyone may <i>add</i> <a href="/wiki/Template:Trademarked" title="Template:Trademarked"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{Trademarked}}</span></a>. You should be explicit about whose trademark it is. - <a href="/wiki/User:Jmabel" title="User:Jmabel">Jmabel</a>&nbsp;! <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jmabel" title="User talk:Jmabel">talk</a> 18:03, 4 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
       </ul> 
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           @<a href="/wiki/User:Jmabel" title="User:Jmabel">Jmabel</a>:Thanks. But can/should I replace the <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-self" title="Template:PD-self">Template:PD-self</a> with <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-shape" title="Template:PD-shape">Template:PD-shape</a>? I mean this kind of pattern should have been ineligible for copyright, so the user should not have the right to "release this work into the public domain". Although both templates declare images into public domain.--<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:%E7%AB%8B%E6%97%A5&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:??            <dl>
            <dd>
             @<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:%E7%AB%8B%E6%97%A5&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:?? (page does not exist)">??</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:%E7%AB%8B%E6%97%A5&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:?? (page does not exist)">??</a>: I don't think it matters much. Creator is saying via <a href="/wiki/Template:PD-self" title="Template:PD-self"><span style="font-family:monospace,monospace;">{{PD-self}}</span></a>, "I relinquish my rights in this." If there were no rights to relinquish, then we are in the same place. - <a href="/wiki/User:Jmabel" title="User:Jmabel">Jmabel</a>&nbsp;! <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jmabel" title="User talk:Jmabel">talk</a> 00:48, 5 June 2021 (UTC)
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </dd>
         </dl>
        </dd>
       </dl>
